< review>
This dog park is new to me, although it has clearly been around for a while. For example, the fencing has clearly been repaired more than once, and the tall brick wall that separates the highway from the dog park has a couple of painted over patches to hide graffiti. However, the park itself is probably almost a quarter of an acre, and has big old trees, fresh water available, real grass!, lots of shade and places to sit for the humans, and (from what I can tell) a friendly and welcoming community. Oddly, the small dog park is just a shadeless, fenced-in patch of spiky sand. I've seen fast running dogs actually tear up their paws on that sand, so I don't know why anyone would want to use it! Stick to the large dog park - it's beautiful and I highly recommend it. Also, if you want to, you can leash your dog and walk around with them in the rest of the park - there's a small lake at the other end, lots of trees and greenery, curving paths, picnic tables, and other nice stuff. It's generally just a very pleasant looking place.

Later edit: now I know what the smaller, grassless section of dog park is for - they use it for the dogs to run and play in when the large, grassy part is very wet and/or muddy. I think this is great -- it means that the grassy Park stays grassy rather than becoming a torn up mud pit. The rangers make sure it all stays nice too, which I appreciate. Still an excellent park for dogs!<//review>

By San Jose standards, this facility is awesome. Separate areas for large and small dogs; double gated; fresh water; real grass; ENORMOUS fenced area; lots of shade; big trees. The only problem is...there's often no dogs. What fun is that? This place is usually empty because you either need to pay an entrance fee to Hellyer park or park your car in front of someone's house in a nearby neighborhood.</review>

< Text>
This is one of my most favorite thrift shops. Whenever I am over in Angels Camp I make it a point to ALWAYS stop in and I never leave empty handed.

The employee's are terrific! The merchandise is fantastic! The prices are amazing! And the store is so well organized!

On the first few days of every month statewide 1/2 price sale. You cannot beat that!

Make sure to stop in and check things out for yourselves. I promise you will not be disappointed that you did.

<username>MikeyMo82</username><Time>1527715587046< /Time><Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
I've been going to the brewery for a decade. So I guess I like the place, right? Yeah, I do. I mean they have root beer on tap (which totally just pushed my rating to five stars). Who doesn't think that is awesome? The food menu has a lot of options. Like, more than most restaurants. Burgers are good, sandwiches are damn fine, the salads are big and tasty. But man, those NACHOS, BRO! Those things are top tier buddy.
Moving along to the beer: Matt brews a dozen or more beers in house, somewhere between five and seven of which will be available on any given day. My favorites: Strawberry Blond (wheat), Dead Head Red (Red), Red Leaf (2xIPA), Trainwreck (IPA), Pirate Porter (brewed with rum). I could go on and on. They also have a bunch of guest taps that have various popular beers. Staff is, like, the best too.< /Review>

< Text>
This is a great neighborhood bar and grill.  It's not sports bar, though you can catch a game every once in awhile. Live bands on Friday nights provide a fun environment for the 30+ crowd.

The staff and owners are friendly and attentive.

Food is good. Drinks are good,  but a little pricey. My favorite is the BBQ chicken Quesadilla.

Definitely a place worth checking out.</Text>

Charges you for expensive beers you didn't order.

Avoid this place.<//Review>

Love the food and beers, service is usually solid. Occasionally we run into a shortage of indoor seating due to truly reserved tables (locked off a good 20-30min ahead of the reservation). I guess that's ok if it's your reservation, but it hurts the experience for walk-ins. Outdoor seating is fun, though super hot in the earlier summer evenings, and the sun glares pretty hard at you until it disappears below the facade of the old Pleasanton Hotel building across the street.<//review>

< date>
1508172628590<//date>
<Rating>4< /Rating>< Text>
Great local hangout with a very good selection of beers and live music on weekends.
Downgraded one star for hit and miss food quality, charging full price for ice tea refills and for high turnover of waitstaff.
We've been here several times over the past few months and have had several waitresses tell us it's their first day or week.
The food has been hit and miss, whether ordering the same item or something different there is no consistency to the quality. The first time I had the garlic mushroom burger it was awesome! Cooked just right and flavorful.  I ordered it again on my most recent visit and it was cooked to death! It was flavorless and tough to chew.
A while back the band was pretty good so we stayed for the band's entire show. We had two appetizers, two dinners with ice tea to drink and I had two glasses of beer. Neither one of us drinks alcohol much for health reasons. Throughout the night we both had refills of ice tea.  When the bill came I was surprised to see that we were being charged full price for every ice tea refill.  This charge took a what should have been a reasonable bill for dinner into the realm of absurdly expensive.
I paid the bill and noted on the receipt my dissatisfaction at the outrageous charge for ice tea refills. We frequently dine out and very few restaurants charge for ice tea refills.  Those that do usually print this fact on the menu or the waitperson informs patrons that refills are charged for, typically at a nominal price much less than the full price, usually less than half price.
We still like the Main Street Brewery  and will continue to patronize the business in the hope that management reads this review and makes the appropriate adjustments.< /Text>

< review>
Well priced, great tasting sushi for downtown SF. The entrees are a little pricier, but definitely not outrageous or out of the budget for someone going to a sushi place.

The service was also pretty good! The waitress greeted us almost immediately and made sure we constantly had a mug full of tea. She wasn't as great about refilling the waters (it was a SUPER hot day, we weren't so much about the hot tea...) but other than that not bad!

Parking was also fairly easy to find, but it might've just been because of what time we went (early dinner on a weekday) so don't take that advice to heart too much!

Overall well-priced food in a good location.</review>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
This is my go to sushi place from now on.

As expected, a sushi place with this high of a rating is always full, what's great about it though is their service is constant and their food is always good. It seems that however rushed they are their food always seem to be great. I personally always go here with 1 or 2 friends and not much more since the place is a bit cozy and having a big group doesn't really seem to be recommended. Whenever I go we usually get either the Omakase or the Lover's boat since both are great for 2 people. Although of its your first time, I'd suggest getting the omakase for solo, all of the dishes that the chef serves is amazing!

Lastly if you live near this place or have a safe way to get home, their sake choices are great and itsi a great way to slow down the fast day that you've been through.

Overall great place and probably the only restaurant that I've given a full 5 stars to, and rightfully so.</Review>

Love this restaurant. They have some of the best sashimi in the Bay Area and is reasonably priced. My wife and I went here for lunch on Valentine's Day and the placed was packed. Luckily, a few tables were finished and ready to leave. We end waiting for less then thirty minutes. We ordered baby o toro, hamachi toro, sake tore, uni and Hokkaido scallops. We have the hamachi toro lightly seared, which give a more complex taste.</Review>

< text>
Short story: Good sushi. HORRENDIOUS service. Will NOT be back.

Long story: Searched Google for a good sushi restaurant while in town. Found Amami San accessible, reasonably priced and great reviews. My fianc√© and I arrived a little before 7pm and it was packed - a good sign for good sushi, which we were craving and in no particular rush so, we waited patiently close to 20 minutes before it was blatantly obvious the hostess/waitress was ignoring us and another party of four - I'm assuming in hopes that we would tire of waiting and move along to another place. But, as I said before we were in no rush and the packed house solidified this was the place to be for good sushi. The group of four was seated and we watched as 2, 3, then 4 tables became available and still no acknowledgement from the h/w. A woman, a couple, and a trio walk in and within 30 seconds the h/w walks up and addresses the couple first (seriously?!), before finally getting us on the list and sitting us a few minutes later. Trying to give them the benefit of the doubt, we sit down at the sushi bar excited to get some food. The trio is sat beside us almost immediately. We decide on some misos to start and 4 rolls to share. Waitress comes back in 5 minutes or so and we place our order and get our misos relatively quickly. The satisfaction of warm tasty miso quickly evaporates as 10.... 20 minutes go by and the trio next to us starts getting food but no sign of our rolls. 30... 40 minutes have passed and more food gets passed over us at the bar to the waitresses running it out to tables AND more annoyingly to the trio beside us. Sushi chef behind the bar asks if we had ordered as he hands another plate of food to another couple beside us. Yes. Yes we have. (Add insult to injury as my stomach is eating itself) 50... 60 minutes has now gone by and I am one platter away from leaving a $10 on the table and walking out the door. Thankfully next plate up is two of our rolls. We devour them, wait another 10 minutes for our last two rolls and inhale them in 30 seconds. Card out, we try (and fail) to get our waitresses' attention to grab the check. My much nicer and more patient fianc√© finally gets her attention and she brings the check but walks off before he can open the black book to put his card into (which he already had out and in his hand). 5 minutes later, we finally stand up to hand them our bill so we can leave. Our waitress comes and grabs our check as we are noticeably standing in the front of this small establishment, but a different waitress brings our check back and rudely drops it (with an audible 'smack') on the counter in front of us without a word. Relieved to leave after taking over 2 hours, we will never be back because of the lack of communication and outright disrespectful service.<//text>

< rating>
4< /rating>
< text>
This restaurant is actually just for the most part, an average place. Average service, and average food. Everything is just average, apart from the "Omakase."

This single dish makes stopping at this restaurant worth it. For the uninitiated, or for those who don't really go for sushi, "Omakase" or "„Åä„Åæ„Åã„Åõ", is roughly translated as "Depend on you," but in a restaurant, it means that you're letting the chef choose. And that's exactly what they do, and they do it well.

This also means that I can't tell you what pieces you'll get, as it changes with time. Admittedly, this dish is pricey, but every now and then, it's worth it.

Also, it should be noted that the last time I was here, a friend of mine waited more than 30 minutes for 2 orders of tuna nigiri, with confirmation of the dish twice.

Understandably he ended up cancelling it in the end because it never came. Even though they were busy, it's funny that they couldn't get a few pieces to him within that time frame. He should have gone with an Omakase.< /text>
